# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

Perfect! I've successfully identified and documented all the Rust source files that implement the async runtime waker mechanism in rust-lang/rust. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Findings

I identified **8 main source files** that form the core of Rust's async runtime waker mechanism:

### Core Waker System
- **`library/core/src/task/wake.rs`** - Contains the fundamental types:
  - `RawWaker` and `RawWakerVTable` (the low-level vtable-based mechanism)
  - `Waker` (thread-safe wrapper, Send + Sync)
  - `LocalWaker` (single-threaded variant)
  - `Context` and `ContextBuilder` (execution context passed to futures)

- **`library/alloc/src/task.rs`** - Memory-safe trait implementations:
  - `Wake` trait (for constructing Wakers from Arc)
  - `LocalWake` trait (for constructing LocalWakers from Rc)
  - `raw_waker()` and `local_raw_waker()` functions that construct RawWaker vtables

### Future Polling Mechanism
- **`library/core/src/future/future.rs`** - The `Future` trait with the `poll()` method
- **`library/core/src/future/poll_fn.rs`** - `poll_fn()` for creating futures from closures
- **`library/core/src/future/mod.rs`** - Module exports and `ResumeTy` type

### Supporting Types
- **`library/core/src/task/poll.rs`** - `Poll` enum (Ready/Pending)
- **`library/core/src/task/ready.rs`** - `ready!` macro utility
- **`library/core/src/task/mod.rs`** - Task module exports

The answer has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with all files, key symbols (types and functions), the execution chain, and a detailed narrative explaining how these components work together to implement Rust's efficient async/await system.

\\\"const_waker\\\", since = \\\"1.82.0\\\")]\\n236:     #[must_use]\\n237:     #[inline]\\n238:     pub const fn from_waker(waker: &'a Waker) -> Self {\\n239:         ContextBuilder::from_waker(waker).build()\\n240:     }\\n241: \\n242:     /// Returns a reference to the [`Waker`] for the current task.\\n243:     #[inline]\\n244:     #[must_use]\\n245: Waker {\\n248:         &self.waker\\n249:     }\\n250: \\n251:     /// Returns a reference to the [`LocalWaker`] for the current task.\\n252:     #[inline]\\n253:     #[unstable(feature = \\\"local_waker\\\", issue = \\\"118959\\\")]\\n254:     pub const fn local_waker(&self) -> &'a LocalWaker {\\n255:         &self.local_waker\\n256:     }\\n257: \\n258:     /// Returns a reference to    .local_waker(&local_waker)\\n292: ///     .build();\\n293: ///\\n294: /// let mut future = std::pin::pin!(async { 20 });\\n295: /// let poll = future.as_mut().poll(&mut cx);\\n296: /// assert_eq!(poll, Poll::Ready(20));\\n297: ///\\n298: /// ```\\n299: #[unstable(feature = \\\"local_waker\\\", issue = \\\"118959\\\")]\\n300: #[derive(Debug)]\\n301: pub struct ContextBuilder<'a> {\\n302:     waker: &'a Waker,\\n303:     local_waker: &'a LocalWaker,\\n304:     ext: ExtData<'a>,\\n305:     // Ensure we future-proof against variance changes by forcing\\n306:     // the lifetime to be invariant (argument-position lifetimes\\n307:     // are contravariant while return-position lifetimes are\\n308:     // covariant).\\n309:     _marker: PhantomData<fn(&'a ()) -> &'a ()>,\\n310:     // Ensure `Context` is `!Send` and `!Sync` in order to allow\\n311:     // for future `!Send` and / or `!Sync` fields.\\n312:     _marker2: PhantomData<*mut ()>,\\n313: }\\n314: \\n315: impl<'a> ContextBuilder<'a> {\\n316:     /// Creates a ContextBuilder from a Waker.\\n317:     #[inline]\\n318:     #[unstable(feature = \\\"local_waker\\\", issue = \\\"118959\\\")]\\n319:     pub const fn {\\n323:             waker,\\n324:             local_waker,\\n325:             ext: ExtData::None(()),\\n326:             _marker: PhantomData,\\n327:             _marker2: PhantomData,\\n328:         }\\n329:     }\\n330: \\n331:     /// Creates a ContextBuilder from an existing Context.\\n332:     #[inline]\\n333:     #[unstable(feature = \\\"context_ext\\\", issue = \\\"123392\\\")]\\n334:     pub const fn from(cx: &'a mut Context<'_>) -> Self {\\n335:         let ext = match &mut cx.ext.0 {\\n336:             ExtData::Some(ext) => ExtData::Some(*ext),\\n337:             ExtData::None(()) => ExtData::None(()),\\n338:         };\\n339:         Self {\\n340:             waker: cx.waker,\\n341:             local_waker: cx.local_waker,\\n342:             ext,\\n343:             _marker: /// Sets the value for the local waker on `Context`.\\n356:     #[inline]\\n357:     #[unstable(feature = \\\"local_waker\\\", issue = \\\"118959\\\")]\\n358:     pub const fn local_waker(self, local_waker: &'a LocalWaker) -> Self {\\n359:         Self { local_waker, ..self }\\n360:     }\\n361: \\n362:     /// Sets the value for the extension data on `Context`.\\n363:     #[inline]\\n364:     #[unstable(feature = \\\"context_ext\\\", issue = \\\"123392\\\")]\\n365:     pub const fn ext(self, data: &'a mut dyn Any) -> Self {\\n366:         Self { ext: ExtData::Some(data), ..self }\\n367:     }\\n368: \\n369:     /// Builds the `Context`.\\n370:     #[inline]\\n371:     #[unstable(feature = \\\"local_waker\\\", issue = \\\"118959\\\")]\\n372:     pub const fn build(self) -> Context<'a> {\\n373:         let ContextBuilder { waker, local_waker, ext, _marker, _marker2 } = self;\\n374:         Context { waker, local_waker, ext: AssertUnwindSafe(ext), _marker, _marker2 }\\n375:     }\\n376: }\\n377: \\n378: /// A `Waker` is a handle for waking up a task by notifying its executor that it\\n379: /// is ready to be run.\\n380: ///\\n381: /// This handle encapsulates a [`RawWaker`] instance, which defines the\\n382: /// executor-specific wakeup behavior.\\n383: ///\\n384: /// The typical life of a `Waker` is that it is constructed by an executor, wrapped in a\\n385: /// [`Context`], then passed to [`Future::poll()`]. Then, if the future chooses to return\\n386: /// [`Poll::Pending`], it must also store the waker somehow and call [`Waker::wake()`] when\\n387: /// the future should be polled again.\\n388: ///\\n389: /// Implements [`Clone`], [`Send`], and [`Sync`]; therefore, a waker may be invoked\\n390: /// from any thread, including ones not in any way managed by the executor. For example,\\n391: /// this might be done to wake a future when a blocking function call completes on another\\n392: /// thread.\\n393: ///\\n394: /// Note that it is preferable to use `waker.clone_from(&new_waker)` instead\\n395: /// of `*waker = new_waker.clone()`, as the former will avoid cloning the waker\\n396: /// unnecessarily if the two wakers [wake the same task](Self::will_wake).\\n397: ///\\n398: /// Constructing a `Waker` from a [`RawWaker`] is unsafe.\\n399: /// Implementing the [`Wake`] trait is a safe alternative that requires memory allocation.\\n400: ///\\n401: /// [`Future::poll()`]: core::future::Future::poll\\n402: /// [`Poll::Pending`]: core::task::Poll::Pending\\n403: /// [`Wake`]: ../../alloc/task/trait.Wake.html\\n404: #[repr(transparent)]\\n405: #[stable(feature = \\\"futures_api\\\", since = \\\"1.36.0\\\")]\\n406: #[rustc_diagnostic_item = \\\"Waker\\\"]\\n407: pub struct Waker {\\n408:     waker: RawWaker,\\n409: }\\n410: \\n411: #[stable(feature = \\\"futures_api\\\", since = \\\"1.36.0\\\")]\\n412: impl Unpin for Waker {}\\n413: #[stable(feature = \\\"futures_api\\\", since = \\\"1.36.0\\\")]\\n414: unsafe impl Send for Waker {}\\n415: #[stable(feature = \\\"futures_api\\\", since = \\\"1.36.0\\\")]\\n416: unsafe impl Sync for Waker {}\\n417: \\n418: impl Waker {\\n419:     /// Wakes up the task associated with this `Waker`.\\n420:     ///\\n421:     /// As long as the executor keeps running and the task is not finished, it is\\n422:     /// guaranteed that each invocation of [`wake()`](Self::wake) (or\\n423:     /// [`wake_by_ref()`](Self::wake_by_ref)) will be followed by at least one\\n424:     /// [`poll()`] of the task to which this `Waker` belongs. This makes\\n425:     /// it possible to temporarily yield to other tasks while running potentially\\n426:     /// unbounded processing loops.\\n427:     ///\\n428:     /// Note that the above implies that multiple wake-ups may be coalesced into a\\n429:     /// single [`poll()`] invocation by the runtime.\\n430:     ///\\n431:     /// Also note that yielding to competing tasks is not guaranteed: it is the\\n432:     /// executor\u2019s choice which task to run and the executor may choose to run the\\n433:     /// current task again.\\n434:     ///\\n435:     /// [`poll()`]: crate::future::Future::poll\\n436:     #[inline]\\n437:     #[stable(feature = \\\"futures_api\\\", since = \\\"1.36.0\\\")]\\n438:     pub fn wake(self) {\\n439:         // The actual wakeup call is delegated through a virtual function call\\n440:         // to the implementation which is defined by the executor.\\n441: \\n442:         // Don't call `drop` -- the waker will be consumed by `wake`.\\n443:         let this = ManuallyDrop::new(self);\\n444: \\n445:         // SAFETY: This is safe because `Waker::from_raw` is the only way\\n446:         // to initialize `wake` and `data` requiring the user to acknowledge\\n447:         // that the contract of `RawWaker` is upheld.\\n448:         unsafe { (this.waker.vtable.wake)(this.waker.data) };\\n449:     }\\n450: \\n451:     /// Wakes up the task associated with this `Waker` without consuming the `Waker`.\\n452:     ///\\n453:     /// This is similar to [`wake()`](Self::wake), but may be slightly less efficient in\\n454:     /// the case where an owned `Waker` is available. This method should be preferred to\\n455:     /// calling `waker.clone().wake()`.\\n456:     #[inline]\\n457:     #[stable(feature = \\\"futures_api\\\", since = \\\"1.36.0\\\")]\\n458:     pub fn wake_by_ref(&self) {\\n459:         // The actual wakeup call is delegated through a virtual function call\\n460:         // to the implementation which is defined by the executor.\\n461: \\n462:         // SAFETY: see `wake`\\n463:         unsafe { (self.waker.vtable.wake_by_ref)(self.waker.data) }\\n464:     }\\n465: \\n466:     /// Returns `true` if this `Waker` and another `Waker` would awake the same task.\\n467:     ///\\n468:     /// This function works on a best-effort basis, and may return false even\\n469:     /// when the `Waker`s would awaken the same task. However, if this function\\n470:     /// returns `true`, it is guaranteed that the `Waker`s will awaken the same task.\\n471:     ///\\n472:     /// This function is primarily used for optimization purposes \u2014 for example,\\n473:     /// this type's [`clone_from`](Self::clone_from) implementation uses it to\\n474:     /// avoid cloning the waker when they would wake the same task anyway.\\n475:     #[inline]\\n476:     #[must_use]\\n477:     #[stable(feature = \\\"futures_api\\\", since = \\\"1.36.0\\\")]\\n478:     pub fn will_wake(&self, other: &Waker) -> bool {\\n479:         // We optimize this by comparing vtable addresses instead of vtable contents.\\n480:         // This is permitted since the function is documented as best-effort.\\n481:         let RawWaker { data: a_data, vtable: a_vtable } = self.waker;\\n482:         let RawWaker { data: b_data, vtable: b_vtable } = other.waker;\\n483:         a_data == b_data && ptr::eq(a_vtable, b_vtable)\\n484:     }\\n485: \\n486:     /// Creates a new `Waker` from the provided `data` pointer and `vtable`.\\n487:     ///\\n488:     /// The `data` pointer can be used to store arbitrary data as required\\n489:     /// by the executor. This could be e.g. a type-erased pointer to an `Arc`\\n490:     /// that is associated with the task.\\n491:     /// The value of this pointer will get passed to all functions that are part\\n492:     /// of the `vtable` as the first parameter.\\n493:     ///\\n494:     /// It is important to consider that the `data` pointer must point to a\\n495:     /// thread safe type such as an `Arc`.\\n496:     ///\\n497:     /// The `vtable` customizes the behavior of a `Waker`. For each operation\\n498:     /// on the `Waker`, the associated function in the `vtable` will be called.\\n499:     ///\\n500:     /// # Safety\\n501:     ///\\n502:     /// The behavior of the returned `Waker` is undefined if the contract defined\\n503:     /// in [`RawWakerVTable`]'s documentation is not upheld.\\n504:     ///\\n505:     /// (Authors wishing to avoid unsafe code may implement the [`Wake`] trait instead, at the\\n506:     /// cost of a required heap allocation.)\\n507:     ///\\n508:     /// [`Wake`]: ../../alloc/task/trait.Wake.html\\n509:     #[inline]\\n510:     #[must_use]\\n511:     #[stable(feature = \\\"waker_getters\\\", since = \\\"1.83.0\\\")]\\n512:     #[rustc_const_stable(feature = \\\"waker_getters\\\", since = \\\"1.83.0\\\")]\\n513:     pub const unsafe fn new(data: *const (), vtable: &'static RawWakerVTable) -> Self {\\n514:         Waker { waker: RawWaker { data, vtable } }\\n515:     }\\n516: \\n517:     /// Creates a new `Waker` from [`RawWaker`].\\n518:     ///\\n519:     /// # Safety\\n520:     ///\\n521:     /// The behavior of the returned `Waker` is undefined if the contract defined\\n522:     /// in [`RawWaker`]'s and [`RawWakerVTable`]'s documentation is not upheld.\\n523:     ///\\n524:     /// (Authors wishing to avoid unsafe code may implement the [`Wake`] trait instead, at the\\n525:     /// cost of a required heap allocation.)\\n526:     ///\\n527:     /// [`Wake`]: ../../alloc/task/trait.Wake.html\\n528:     #[inline]\\n529:     #[must_use]\\n530:     #[stable(feature = \\\"futures_api\\\", since = \\\"1.36.0\\\")]\\n531:     #[rustc_const_stable(feature = \\\"const_waker\\\", since = \\\"1.82.0\\\")]\\n532:     pub const unsafe fn from_raw(waker: RawWaker) -> Waker {\\n533:         Waker { waker }\\n534:     }\\n535: \\n536:     /// Returns a reference to a `Waker` that does nothing when used.\\n537:     ///\\n538:     // Note!  Much of the documentation for this method is duplicated\\n539:     // in the docs for `LocalWaker::noop`.\\n540:     // If you edit it, consider editing the other copy too.\\n541:     //\\n542:     /// This is mostly useful for writing tests that need a [`Context`] to poll\\n543:     /// some futures, but are not expecting those futures to wake the waker or\\n544:     /// do not need to do anything specific if it happens.\\n545:     ///\\n546:     /// More generally, using `Waker::noop()` to poll a future\\n547:     /// means discarding the notification of when the future should be polled again.\\n548:     /// So it should only be used when such a notification will not be needed to make progress.\\n549:     ///\\n550:     /// If an owned `Waker` is needed, `clone()` this task::Context::from_waker(task::Waker::noop());\\n559:     ///\\n560:     /// let mut future = Box::pin(async { 10 });\\n561:     /// assert_eq!(future.as_mut().poll(&mut cx), task::Poll::Ready(10));\\n562:     /// ```\\n563:     #[inline]\\n564:     #[must_use]\\n565:     #[stable(feature = \\\"noop_waker\\\", since = \\\"1.85.0\\\")]\\n566:     #[rustc_const_stable(feature = \\\"noop_waker\\\", since = \\\"1.85.0\\\")]\\n567:     pub const fn noop() -> &'static Waker {\\n568:         const WAKER: &Waker = &Waker { waker: RawWaker::NOOP };\\n569:         WAKER\\n570:     }\\n571: \\n572:     /// Gets the `data` pointer used to create this `Waker`.\\n573:     #[inline]\\n574:     #[must_use]\\n575:     #[stable(feature = \\\"waker_getters\\\", since = \\\"1.83.0\\\")]\\n576:     pub fn data(&self) -> *const () {\\n577:         self.waker.data\\n578:     }\\n579: \\n580:     /// Gets the `vtable` pointer used to create this `Waker`.\\n581:     #[inline]\\n582:     #[must_use]\\n583:     #[stable(feature = \\\"waker_getters\\\", since = \\\"1.83.0\\\")]\\n584:     pub fn vtable(&self) -> &'static RawWakerVTable {\\n585:         self.waker.vtable\\n586:     }\\n587: \\n588:     /// Constructs a `Waker` from a function pointer.\\n589:     #[inline]\\n590:     #[must_use]\\n591:     #[unstable(feature = \\\"waker_from_fn_ptr\\\", issue = \\\"148457\\\")]\\n592:     pub const fn from_fn_ptr(f: fn()) -> Self {\\n593:         // SAFETY: Unsafe is used for transmutes, pointer came from `fn()` so it\\n594:         //         is sound to transmute it back to `fn()`.\\n595:         static VTABLE: RawWakerVTable = unsafe {\\n596:             RawWakerVTable::new(\\n597:                 |this| RawWaker::new(this, &VTABLE),\\n598:                 |this| transmute::<*const (), fn()>(this)(),\\n599:                 |this| transmute::<*const (), fn()>(this)(),\\n600:                 |_| {},\\n601:             )\\n602:         };\\n603:         let raw = RawWaker::new(f as *const (), &VTABLE);\\n604: \\n605:         // SAFETY: `clone` is just a copy, `drop` is a no-op while `wake` and\\n606:         //         `wake_by_ref` just call the function pointer.\\n607:         unsafe { Self::from_raw(raw) }\\n608:     }\\n609: }\\n610: \\n611: #[stable(feature = \\\"futures_api\\\", since = \\\"1.36.0\\\")]\\n612: impl Clone for Waker {\\n613:     #[inline]\\n614:     fn clone(&self) -> Self {\\n615:         Waker {\\n616:             // SAFETY: This is safe because `Waker::from_raw` is the only way\\n617:             // to initialize `clone` and `data` requiring the user to acknowledge\\n618:             // that the contract of [`RawWaker`] is upheld.\\n619:             waker: unsafe { (self.waker.vtable.clone)(self.waker.data) },\\n620:         }\\n621:     }\\n622: \\n623:     /// Assigns a clone of `source` to `self`, unless [`self.will_wake(source)`][Waker::will_wake] anyway.\\n624:     ///\\n625:     /// This method is preferred over simply assigning `source.clone()` to `self`,\\n626:     /// as it avoids cloning the waker if `self` is already the same waker.\\n627:     ///\\n628:     /// # Examples\\n629:     ///\\n630:     /// ```\\n631:     /// use std::future::Future;\\n632:     /// use std::pin::Pin;\\n633:     /// use std::sync::{Arc, Mutex};\\n634:     /// use std::task::{Context, Poll, Waker};\\n635:     ///\\n636:     /// struct Waiter {\\n637:     ///     shared: Arc<Mutex<Shared>>,\\n638:     /// }\\n639:     ///\\n640:     /// struct Shared {\\n641:     ///     waker: Waker,\\n642:     ///     // ...\\n643:     /// }\\n644:     ///\\n645:     /// impl Future for Waiter {\\n646:     ///     type Output = ();\\n647:     ///     fn poll(self: Pin<&mut Self>, cx: &mut Context<'_>) -> Poll<()> {\\n648:     ///         let mut shared = self.shared.lock().unwrap();\\n649:     ///\\n650:     ///         // update the waker\\n651:     ///         shared.waker.clone_from(cx.waker());\\n652:     ///\\n653:     ///         // readiness logic ...\\n654:     /// #       Poll::Ready(())\\n655:     ///     }\\n656:     /// }\\n657:     ///\\n658:     /// ```\\n659:     #[inline]\\n660:     fn clone_from(&mut self, source: &Self) {\\n661:         if !self.will_wake(source) {\\n662:             *self = source.clone();\\n663:         }\\n664:     }\\n665: }\\n666: \\n667: #[stable(feature = \\\"futures_api\\\", since = \\\"1.36.0\\\")]\\n668: impl Drop for Waker {\\n669:     #[inline]\\n670:     fn drop(&mut self) {\\n671:         // SAFETY: This is safe because `Waker::from_raw` is the only way\\n672:         // to initialize `drop` and `data` requiring the user to acknowledge\\n673:         // that the contract of `RawWaker` is upheld.\\n674:         unsafe { (self.waker.vtable.drop)(self.waker.data) }\\n675:     }\\n676: }\\n677: \\n678: #[stable(feature = \\\"futures_api\\\", since = \\\"1.36.0\\\")]\\n679: impl fmt::Debug for Waker {\\n680:     fn fmt(&self, f: &mut fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> fmt::Result {\\n681:         let vtable_ptr = self.waker.vtable as *const RawWakerVTable;\\n682:         f.debug_struct(\\\"Waker\\\")\\n683:             .field(\\\"data\\\", &self.waker.data)\\n684:             .field(\\\"vtable\\\", &vtable_ptr)\\n685:             .finish()\\n686:     }\\n687: }\\n688: \\n689: /// A `LocalWaker` is analogous to a [`Waker`], but it does not implement [`Send`] or [`Sync`].\\n690: ///\\n691: /// This handle encapsulates a [`RawWaker`] instance, which defines the\\n692: /// executor-specific wakeup behavior.\\n693: ///\\n694: /// Local wakers can be requested from a `Context` with the [`local_waker`] method.\\n695: ///\\n696: /// The typical life of a `LocalWaker` is that it is constructed by an executor, wrapped in a\\n697: /// [`Context`] using [`ContextBuilder`], then passed to [`Future::poll()`]. Then, if the future chooses to return\\n698: /// [`Poll::Pending`], it must also store the waker somehow and call [`LocalWaker::wake()`] when\\n699: /// the future should be polled again.\\n700: ///\\n701: /// Implements [`Clone`], but neither [`Send`] nor [`Sync`]; therefore, a local waker may\\n702: /// not be moved to other threads. In general, when deciding to use wakers or local wakers,\\n703: /// local wakers are preferable unless the waker needs to be sent across threads. This is because\\n704: /// wakers can incur in additional cost related to memory synchronization.\\n705: ///\\n706: /// Note that it is preferable to use `local_waker.clone_from(&new_waker)` instead\\n707: /// of `*local_waker = new_waker.clone()`, as the former will avoid cloning the waker\\n708: /// unnecessarily if the two wakers [wake the same task](Self::will_wake).\\n709: ///\\n710: /// # Examples\\n711: /// Usage of a local waker to implement a future analogous to `std::thread::yield_now()`.\\n712: /// ```\\n713: /// #![feature(local_waker)]\\n714: /// use std::future::{Future, poll_fn};\\n715: /// use std::task::Poll;\\n716: ///\\n717: /// // a future that returns pending once.\\n718: /// fn yield_now() -> impl Future<Output=()> + Unpin {\\n719: ///     let mut yielded = false;\\n720: ///     poll_fn(move |cx| {\\n721: ///         if !yielded {\\n722: ///             yielded = true;\\n723: ///             cx.local_waker().wake_by_ref();\\n724: ///             return Poll::Pending;\\n725: ///         }\\n726: ///         return Poll::Ready(())\\n727: ///     })\\n728: /// }\\n729: ///\\n730: /// # async fn __() {\\n731: /// yield_now().await;\\n732: /// # }\\n733: /// ```\\n734: ///\\n735: /// [`Future::poll()`]: core::future::Future::poll\\n736: /// [`Poll::Pending`]: core::task::Poll::Pending\\n737: /// [`local_waker`]: core::task::Context::local_waker\\n738: #[unstable(feature = \\\"local_waker\\\", issue = \\\"118959\\\")]\\n739: #[repr(transparent)]\\n740: pub struct LocalWaker {\\n741:     waker: RawWaker,\\n742: }\\n743: \\n744: #[unstable(feature = \\\"local_waker\\\", issue = \\\"118959\\\")]\\n745: impl Unpin for LocalWaker {}\\n746: \\n747: impl LocalWaker {\\n748:     /// Wakes up the task associated with this `LocalWaker`.\\n749:     ///\\n750:     /// As long as the executor keeps running and the task is not finished, it is\\n751:     /// guaranteed that each invocation of [`wake()`](Self::wake) (or\\n752:     /// [`wake_by_ref()`](Self::wake_by_ref)) will be followed by at least one\\n753:     /// [`poll()`] of the task to which this `LocalWaker` belongs. This makes\\n754:     /// it possible to temporarily yield to other tasks while running potentially\\n755:     /// unbounded processing loops.\\n756:     ///\\n757:     /// Note that the above implies that multiple wake-ups may be coalesced into a\\n758:     /// single [`poll()`] invocation by the runtime.\\n759:     ///\\n760:     /// Also note that yielding to competing tasks is not guaranteed: it is the\\n761:     /// executor\u2019s choice which task to run and the executor may choose to run the\\n762:     /// current task again.\\n763:     ///\\n764:     /// [`poll()`]: crate::future::Future::poll\\n765:     #[inline]\\n766:     #[unstable(feature = \\\"local_waker\\\", issue = \\\"118959\\\")]\\n767:     pub fn wake(self) {\\n768:         // The actual wakeup call is delegated through a virtual function call\\n769:         // to the implementation which is defined by the executor.\\n770: \\n771:         // Don't call `drop` -- the waker will be consumed by `wake`.\\n772:         let this = ManuallyDrop::new(self);\\n773: \\n774:         // SAFETY: This is safe because `Waker::from_raw` is the only way\\n775:         // to initialize `wake` and `data` requiring the user to acknowledge\\n776:         // that the contract of `RawWaker` is upheld.\\n777:         unsafe { (this.waker.vtable.wake)(this.waker.data) };\\n778:     }\\n779: \\n780:     /// Wakes up the task associated with this `LocalWaker` without consuming the `LocalWaker`.\\n781:     ///\\n782:     /// This is similar to [`wake()`](Self::wake), but may be slightly less efficient in\\n783:     /// the case where an owned `Waker` is available. This method should be preferred to\\n784:     /// calling `waker.clone().wake()`.\\n785:     #[inline]\\n786:     #[unstable(feature = \\\"local_waker\\\", issue = \\\"118959\\\")]\\n787:     pub fn wake_by_ref(&self) {\\n788:         // The actual wakeup call is delegated through a virtual function call\\n789:         // to the implementation which is defined by the executor.\\n790: \\n791:         // SAFETY: see `wake`\\n792:         unsafe { (self.waker.vtable.wake_by_ref)(self.waker.data) }\\n793:     }\\n794: \\n795:     /// Returns `true` if this `LocalWaker` and another `LocalWaker` would awake the same task.\\n796:     ///\\n797:     /// This function works on a best-effort basis, and may return false even\\n798:     /// when the `Waker`s would awaken the same task. However, if this function\\n799:     /// returns `true`, it is guaranteed that the `Waker`s will awaken the same task.\\n800:     ///\\n801:     /// This function is primarily used for optimization purposes \u2014 for example,\\n802:     /// this type's [`clone_from`](Self::clone_from) implementation uses it to\\n803:     /// avoid cloning the waker when they would wake the same task anyway.\\n804:     #[inline]\\n805:     #[must_use]\\n806:     #[unstable(feature = \\\"local_waker\\\", issue = \\\"118959\\\")]\\n807:     pub fn will_wake(&self, other: &LocalWaker) -> bool {\\n808:         // We optimize this by comparing vtable addresses instead of vtable contents.\\n809:         // This is permitted since the function is documented as best-effort.\\n810:         let RawWaker { data: a_data, vtable: a_vtable } = self.waker;\\n811:         let RawWaker { data: b_data, vtable: b_vtable } = other.waker;\\n812:         a_data == b_data && ptr::eq(a_vtable, b_vtable)\\n813:     }\\n814: \\n815:     /// Creates a new `LocalWaker` from the provided `data` pointer and `vtable`.\\n816:     ///\\n817:     /// The `data` pointer can be used to store arbitrary data as required\\n818:     /// by the executor. This could be e.g. a type-erased pointer to an `Arc`\\n819:     /// that is associated with the task.\\n820:     /// The value of this pointer will get passed to all functions that are part\\n821:     /// of the `vtable` as the first parameter.\\n822:     ///\\n823:     /// The `vtable` customizes the behavior of a `LocalWaker`. For each\\n824:     /// operation on the `LocalWaker`, the associated function in the `vtable`\\n825:     /// will be called.\\n826:     ///\\n827:     /// # Safety\\n828:     ///\\n829:     /// The behavior of the returned `Waker` is undefined if the contract defined\\n830:     /// in [`RawWakerVTable`]'s documentation is not upheld.\\n831:     ///\\n832:     #[inline]\\n833:     #[must_use]\\n834:     #[unstable(feature = \\\"local_waker\\\", issue = \\\"118959\\\")]\\n835:     pub const unsafe fn new(data: *const (), vtable: &'static RawWakerVTable) -> Self {\\n836:         LocalWaker { waker: RawWaker { data, vtable } }\\n837:     }\\n838: \\n839:     /// Creates a new `LocalWaker` from [`RawWaker`].\\n840:     ///\\n841:     /// The behavior of the returned `LocalWaker` is undefined if the contract defined\\n842:     /// in [`RawWaker`]'s and [`RawWakerVTable`]'s documentation is not upheld.\\n843:     /// Therefore this method is unsafe.\\n844:     #[inline]\\n845:     #[must_use]\\n846:     #[unstable(feature = \\\"local_waker\\\", issue = \\\"118959\\\")]\\n847:     pub const unsafe fn from_raw(waker: RawWaker) -> LocalWaker {\\n848:         Self { waker }\\n849:     }\\n850: \\n851:     /// Returns a reference to a `LocalWaker` that does nothing when used.\\n852:     ///\\n853:     // Note!  Much of the documentation for this method is duplicated\\n854:     // in the docs for `Waker::noop`.\\n855:     // If you edit it, consider editing the other copy too.\\n856:     //\\n857:     /// This is mostly useful for writing tests that need a [`Context`] to poll\\n858:     /// some futures, but are not expecting those futures to wake the waker or\\n859:     /// do not need to do anything specific if it happens.\\n860:     ///\\n861:     /// More generally, using `LocalWaker::noop()` to poll a future\\n862:     /// means discarding the notification of when the future should be polled again,\\n863:     /// So it should only be used when such a notification will not be needed to make progress.\\n864:     ///\\n865:     /// If an owned `LocalWaker` is needed, `clone()` this one.\\n866:     ///\\n867:     /// # Examples\\n868:     ///\\n869:     /// ```\\n870:     /// #![feature(local_waker)]\\n871:     /// use std::future::Future;\\n872:     /// use std::task::{ContextBuilder, LocalWaker, Waker, Poll};\\n873:     ///\\n874:     /// let mut cx = ContextBuilder::from_waker(Waker::noop())\\n875:     ///     .local_waker(LocalWaker::noop())\\n876:     ///     .build();\\n877:     ///\\n878:     /// let mut future = Box::pin(async { 10 });\\n879:     /// assert_eq!(future.as_mut().poll(&mut cx), Poll::Ready(10));\\n880:     /// ```\\n881:     #[inline]\\n882:     #[must_use]\\n883:     #[unstable(feature = \\\"local_waker\\\", issue = \\\"118959\\\")]\\n884:     pub const fn noop() -> &'static LocalWaker {\\n885:         const WAKER: &LocalWaker = &LocalWaker { waker: RawWaker::NOOP };\\n886:         WAKER\\n887:     }\\n888: \\n889:     /// Gets the `data` pointer used to create this `LocalWaker`.\\n890:     #[inline]\\n891:     "content": "1: #![stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n2: \n3: use crate::any::Any;\n4: use crate::marker::PhantomData;\n5: use crate::mem::{ManuallyDrop, transmute};\n6: use crate::panic::AssertUnwindSafe;\n7: use crate::{fmt, ptr};\n8: \n9: /// A `RawWaker` allows the implementor of a task executor to create a [`Waker`]\n10: /// or a [`LocalWaker`] which provides customized wakeup behavior.\n11: ///\n12: /// It consists of a data pointer and a [virtual function pointer table (vtable)][vtable]\n13: /// that customizes the behavior of the `RawWaker`.\n14: ///\n15: /// `RawWaker`s are unsafe to use.\n16: /// Implementing the [`Wake`] trait is a safe alternative that requires memory allocation.\n17: ///\n18: /// [vtable]: https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Virtual_method_table\n19: /// [`Wake`]: ../../alloc/task/trait.Wake.html\n20: #[derive(PartialEq, Debug)]\n21: #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n22: pub struct RawWaker {\n23:     /// A data pointer, which can be used to store arbitrary data as required\n24:     /// by the executor. This could be e.g. a type-erased pointer to an `Arc`\n25:     /// that is associated with the task.\n26:     /// The value of this field gets passed to all functions that are part of\n27:     /// the vtable as the first parameter.\n28:     data: *const (),\n29:     /// Virtual function pointer table that customizes the behavior of this waker.\n30:     vtable: &'static RawWakerVTable,\n31: }\n32: \n33: impl RawWaker {\n34:     /// Creates a new `RawWaker` from the provided `data` pointer and `vtable`.\n35:     ///\n36:     /// The `data` pointer can be used to store arbitrary data as required\n37:     /// by the executor. This could be e.g. a type-erased pointer to an `Arc`\n38:     /// that is associated with the task.\n39:     /// The value of this pointer will get passed to all functions that are part\n40:     /// of the `vtable` as the first parameter.\n41:     ///\n42:     /// It is important to consider that the `data` pointer must point to a\n43:     /// thread safe type such as an `Arc<T: Send + Sync>`\n44:     /// when used to construct a [`Waker`]. This restriction is lifted when\n45:     /// constructing a [`LocalWaker`], which allows using types that do not implement\n46:     /// <code>[Send] + [Sync]</code> like `Rc<T>`.\n47:     ///\n48:     /// The `vtable` customizes the behavior of a `Waker` which gets created\n49:     /// from a `RawWaker`. Calling one of the contained functions using\n85: /// any other `data` pointer will cause undefined behavior.\n86: ///\n87: /// Note that while this type implements `PartialEq`, comparing function pointers, and hence\n88: /// comparing structs like this that contain function pointers, is unreliable: pointers to the same\n89: /// function can compare inequal (because functions are duplicated in multiple codegen units), and\n90: /// pointers to *different* functions can compare equal (since identical functions can be\n91: /// deduplicated within a codegen unit).\n92: ///\n93: /// # Thread safety\n94: /// If the [`RawWaker`] will be used to construct a [`Waker`] then\n95: /// these functions must all be thread-safe (even though [`RawWaker`] is\n96: /// <code>\\![Send] + \\![Sync]</code>). This is because [`Waker`] is <code>[Send] + [Sync]</code>,\n97: /// and it may be moved to arbitrary threads or invoked by `&` reference. For example,\n98: /// this means that if the `clone` and `drop` functions manage a reference count,\n99: /// they must do so atomically.\n100: ///\n101: /// However, if the [`RawWaker`] will be used to construct a [`LocalWaker`] instead, then\n102: /// these functions don't need to be thread safe. This means that <code>\\![Send] + \\![Sync]</code>\n103: ///  data can be stored in the data pointer, and reference counting does not need any atomic\n104: /// synchronization.    _marker2: PhantomData<*mut ()>,\n230: }\n231: \n232: impl<'a> Context<'a> {\n233:     /// Creates a new `Context` from a [`&Waker`](Waker).\n234:     #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = {\n239:         ContextBuilder::from_waker(waker).build()\n240:     }\n241: \n242:     /// Returns a reference to the [`Waker`] for the current task.\n243:     #[inline]\n244:     #[must_use]\n245:     #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n246:     #[rustc_const_stable(feature = \"const_waker\", since = \"1.82.0\")]\n247:     pub const fn waker(&self) -> &'a Waker {\n248:         &self.waker\n249:     }\n250: \n251:     /// Returns a reference to the [`LocalWaker`] for the current task.\n252:     #[inline]\n253:     #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n254:     pub const fn local_waker(&self) -> &'a LocalWaker {\n255:         &self.local_waker\n256:     }\n257: \n258:     /// Returns a reference to the extension data for the current task.\n259:     #[inline]\n260:     #[unstable(feature = \"context_ext\", issue = \"123392\")]\n261:     pub const fn ext(&mut self) -> &mut dyn Any {\n262:         // FIXME: this field makes Context extra-weird about unwind safety\n263:         // can we justify AssertUnwindSafe if we stabilize this? do we care?\n264:         match &mut self.ext.0 {\n265:             ExtData::Some(data) => *data,\n266:             ExtData::None(unit) => unit,\n267:         }\n268:     }\n269: }\n270: \n271: #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n272: impl fmt::Debug for Context<'_> {\n273:     fn fmt(&self, f: &mut fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> fmt::Result {\n274:         f.debug_struct(\"Context\").field(\"waker\", &self.waker).finish()\n275:     }\n276: }\n277: \n278: /// A Builder used to construct a `Context` instance\n279: /// with support for `LocalWaker`.\n280: ///\n281: /// # Examples\n282: /// ```\n283: /// #![feature(local_waker)]\n284: /// use std::task::{ContextBuilder, LocalWaker, Waker, Poll};\n285: /// use std::future::Future;\n286: ///\n287: /// let local_waker = LocalWaker::noop();\n288: /// let waker = Waker::noop();\n289: ///\n290: /// let mut cx = ContextBuilder::from_waker(&waker)\n291: ///     .local_waker(&local_waker)\n292: ///     .build();\n293: ///\n294: /// let mut future = std::pin::pin!(async { 20 });\n295: /// let poll = future.as_mut().poll(&mut cx);\n296: /// assert_eq!(poll, Poll::Ready(20));\n297: ///\n298: /// ```\n299: #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n300: #[derive(Debug)]\n301: pub struct ContextBuilder<'a> {\n302:     waker: &'a Waker,\n303:     local_waker: &'a LocalWaker,\n304:     ext: ExtData<'a>,\n305:     // Ensure we future-proof against variance changes by forcing\n306:     // the lifetime to be invariant (argument-position lifetimes\n307:     // are contravariant while return-position lifetimes are\n308:     // covariant).\n309:     _marker: PhantomData<fn(&'a ()) -> &'a ()>,\n310:     // Ensure `Context` is `!Send` and `!Sync` in order to allow\n311:     // for future `!Send` and / or `!Sync` fields.\n312:     _marker2: PhantomData<*mut ()>,\n313: }\n314: \n315: impl<'a> ContextBuilder<'a> {\n316:     /// Creates a ContextBuilder from a Waker.\n317:     #[inline]\n318:     #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n319:     pub const fn from_waker(waker: &'a Waker) -> Self {\n320:         // SAFETY: LocalWaker is just Waker without thread safety\n321:         let local_waker = unsafe { transmute(waker) };\n322:         Self {\n323:             waker,\n324:             local_waker,\n325:             ext: ExtData::None(()),\n326:             _marker: PhantomData,\n327:             _marker2: PhantomData,\n328:         }\n329:     }\n330: \n331:     /// Creates a ContextBuilder from an existing Context.\n332:     #[inline]\n333:     #[unstable(feature = \"context_ext\", issue = \"123392\")]\n334:     pub const fn from(cx: &'a mut Context<'_>) -> Self {\n335:         let ext = match &mut cx.ext.0 {\n336:             ExtData::Some(ext) => ExtData::Some(*ext),\n337:             ExtData::None(()) => ExtData::None(()),\n338:         };\n339:         Self {\n340:             waker: cx.waker,\n341:             local_waker: cx.local_waker,\n342:             ext,\n343:             _marker: PhantomData,\n344:             _marker2: PhantomData,\n345:         }\n346:     }\n347: \n348:     /// Sets the value for the waker on `Context`.\n349:     #[inline]\n350: value for the local waker on `Context`.\n356:     #[inline]\n357:     #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n358:     pub const fn local_waker(self, local_waker: &'a LocalWaker) -> Self {\n359:         Self { local_waker, ..self }\n360:     }\n361: \n362:     /// Sets the value for the extension data on `Context`.\n363:     #[inline]\n364:     #[unstable(feature = \"context_ext\", issue = \"123392\")]\n365:     pub const fn ext(self, data: &'a mut dyn Any) -> Self {\n366:         Self { ext: ExtData::Some(data), ..self }\n367:     }\n368: \n369:     /// Builds the `Context`.\n370:     #[inline]\n371:     #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n372:     pub const fn build(self) -> Context<'a> {\n373:         let ContextBuilder { waker, local_waker, ext, _marker, _marker2 } = self;\n374:         Context { waker, local_waker, ext: AssertUnwindSafe(ext), _marker, _marker2 }\n375:     }\n376: }\n377: \n378: /// A `Waker` is a handle for waking up a task by notifying its executor that it\n379: /// is ready to be run.\n380: ///\n381: /// This handle encapsulates a [`RawWaker`] instance, which defines the\n382: /// executor-specific wakeup behavior.\n383: ///\n384: /// The typical life of a `Waker` is that it is constructed by an executor, wrapped in a\n385: /// [`Context`], then passed to [`Future::poll()`]. Then, if the future chooses to return\n386: /// [`Poll::Pending`], it must also store the waker somehow and call [`Waker::wake()`] when\n387: /// the future should be polled again.\n388: ///\n389: /// Implements [`Clone`], [`Send`], and [`Sync`]; therefore, a waker may be invoked\n390: /// from any thread, including ones not in any way managed by the executor. For example,\n391: /// this might be done to wake a future when a blocking function call completes on another\n392: /// thread.\n393: ///\n394: /// Note that it is preferable to use `waker.clone_from(&new_waker)` instead\n395: /// of `*waker = new_waker.clone()`, as the former will avoid cloning the waker\n396: /// unnecessarily if the two wakers [wake the same task](Self::will_wake).\n397: ///\n398: /// Constructing a `Waker` from a [`RawWaker`] is unsafe.\n399: /// Implementing the [`Wake`] trait is a safe alternative that requires memory allocation.\n400: ///\n401: /// [`Future::poll()`]: core::future::Future::poll\n402: /// [`Poll::Pending`]: core::task::Poll::Pending\n403: /// [`Wake`]: ../../alloc/task/trait.Wake.html\n404: #[repr(transparent)]\n405: #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n406: #[rustc_diagnostic_item = \"Waker\"]\n407: pub struct Waker {\n408:     waker: RawWaker,\n409: }\n410: \n411: #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n412: impl Unpin for Waker {}\n413: #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n414: unsafe impl Send for Waker {}\n415: #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n416: unsafe impl Sync for Waker {}\n417: \n418: impl Waker {\n419:     /// Wakes up the task associated with this `Waker`.\n420:     ///\n421:     /// As long as the executor keeps running and the task is not finished, it is\n422:     /// guaranteed that each invocation of [`wake()`](Self::wake) (or\n423:     /// [`wake_by_ref()`](Self::wake_by_ref)) will be followed by at least one\n424:     /// [`poll()`] of the task to which this `Waker` belongs. This makes\n425:     /// it possible to temporarily yield to other tasks while running potentially\n426:     /// unbounded processing loops.\n427:     ///\n428:     /// Note that the above implies that multiple wake-ups may be coalesced into a\n429:     /// single [`poll()`] invocation by the runtime.\n430:     ///\n431:     /// Also note that yielding to competing tasks is not guaranteed: it is the\n432:     /// executor\u2019s choice which task to run and the executor may choose to run the\n433:     /// current task again.\n434:     ///\n435:     /// [`poll()`]: crate::future::Future::poll\n436:     #[inline]\n437:     #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n438:     pub fn wake(self) {\n439:         // The actual wakeup call is delegated through a virtual function call\n440:         // to the implementation which is defined by the executor.\n441: \n442:         // Don't call `drop` -- the waker will be consumed by `wake`.\n443:         let this = ManuallyDrop::new(self);\n444: \n445:         // SAFETY: This is safe because `Waker::from_raw` is the only way\n446:         // to initialize `wake` and `data` requiring the user to acknowledge\n447:         // that the contract of `RawWaker` is upheld.\n448:         unsafe { (this.waker.vtable.wake)(this.waker.data) };\n449:     }\n450: \n451:     /// Wakes up the task associated with this `Waker` without consuming the `Waker`.\n452:     ///\n453:     /// This is similar to [`wake()`](Self::wake), but may be slightly less efficient in\n454:     /// the case where an owned `Waker` is available. This method should be preferred to\n455:     /// calling `waker.clone().wake()`.\n456:     #[inline]\n457:     #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n458:     pub fn wake_by_ref(&self) {\n459:         // The actual wakeup call is delegated through a virtual function call\n460:         // to the implementation which is defined by the executor.\n461: \n462:         // SAFETY: see `wake`\n463:         unsafe { (self.waker.vtable.wake_by_ref)(self.waker.data) }\n464:     }\n465: \n466:     /// Returns `true` if this `Waker` and another `Waker` would awake the same task.\n467:     ///\n468:     /// This function works on a best-effort basis, and may return false even\n469:     /// when the `Waker`s would awaken the same task. However, if this function\n470:     /// returns `true`, it is guaranteed that the `Waker`s will awaken the same task.\n471:     ///\n472:     /// This function is primarily used for optimization purposes \u2014 for example,\n473:     /// this type's [`clone_from`](Self::clone_from) implementation uses it to\n474:     /// avoid cloning the waker when they would wake the same task anyway.\n475:     #[inline]\n476:     #[must_use]\n477:     #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n478:     pub fn will_wake(&self, other: &Waker) -> bool {\n479:         // We optimize this by comparing vtable addresses instead of vtable contents.\n480:         // This is permitted since the function is documented as best-effort.\n481:         let RawWaker { data: a_data, vtable: a_vtable } = self.waker;\n482:         let RawWaker { data: b_data, vtable: b_vtable } = other.waker;\n483:         a_data == b_data && ptr::eq(a_vtable, b_vtable)\n484:     }\n485: \n486:     /// Creates a new `Waker` from the provided `data` pointer and `vtable`.\n487:     ///\n488:     /// The `data` pointer can be used to store arbitrary data as required\n489:     /// by the executor. This could be e.g. a type-erased pointer to an `Arc`\n490:     /// that is associated with the task.\n491:     /// The value of this pointer will get passed to all functions that are part\n492:     /// of the `vtable` as the first parameter.\n493:     ///\n494:     /// It is important to consider that the `data` pointer must point to a\n495:     /// thread safe type such as an `Arc`.\n496:     ///\n497:     /// The `vtable` customizes the behavior of a `Waker`. For each operation\n498:     /// on the `Waker`, the associated function in the `vtable` will be called.\n499:     ///\n500:     /// # Safety\n501:     ///\n502:     /// The behavior of the returned `Waker` is undefined if the contract defined\n503:     /// in [`RawWakerVTable`]'s documentation is not upheld.\n504:     ///\n505:     /// (Authors wishing to avoid unsafe code may implement the [`Wake`] trait instead, at the\n506:     /// cost of a required heap allocation.)\n507:     ///\n508:     /// [`Wake`]: ../../alloc/task/trait.Wake.html\n509:     #[inline]\n510:     #[must_use]\n511:     #[stable(feature = \"waker_getters\", since = \"1.83.0\")]\n512:     #[rustc_const_stable(feature = \"waker_getters\", since = \"1.83.0\")]\n513:     pub const unsafe fn new(data: *const (), vtable: &'static RawWakerVTable) -> Self {\n514:         Waker { waker: RawWaker { data, vtable } }\n515:     }\n516: \n517:     /// Creates a new `Waker` from [`RawWaker`].\n518:     ///\n519:     /// # Safety\n520:     ///\n521:     /// The behavior of the returned `Waker` is undefined if the contract defined\n522:     /// in [`RawWaker`]'s and [`RawWakerVTable`]'s documentation is not upheld.\n523:     ///\n524:     /// (Authors wishing to avoid unsafe code may implement the [`Wake`] trait instead, at the\n525:     /// cost of a required heap allocation.)\n526:     ///\n527:     /// [`Wake`]: ../../alloc/task/trait.Wake.html\n528:     #[inline]\n529:     #[must_use]\n530:     #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n531:     #[rustc_const_stable(feature = \"const_waker\", since = \"1.82.0\")]\n532:     pub const unsafe fn from_raw(waker: RawWaker) -> Waker {\n533:         Waker { waker }\n534:     }\n535: \n536:     /// Returns a reference to a `Waker` that does nothing when used.\n537:     ///\n538:     // Note!  Much of the documentation for this method is duplicated\n539:     // in the docs for `LocalWaker::noop`.\n540:     // If you edit it, consider editing the other copy too.\n541:     //\n542:     /// This is mostly useful for writing tests that need a [`Context`] to poll\n543:     /// some futures, but are not expecting those futures to wake the waker or\n544:     /// do not need to do anything specific if it happens.\n545:     ///\n546:     /// More generally, using `Waker::noop()` to poll a future\n547:     /// means discarding the notification of when the future should be polled again.\n548:     /// So it should only be used when such a notification will not be needed to make progress.\n549:     ///\n550:     /// If an owned `Waker` is needed, `clone()` this one.\n551:     ///\n552:     /// # Examples\n553:     ///\n554:     /// ```\n555:     /// use std::future::Future;\n556:     /// use std::task;\n557:     ///\n558:     /// let mut cx = task::Context::from_waker(task::Waker::noop());\n559:     ///\n560:     /// let mut future = Box::pin(async { 10 });\n561:     /// assert_eq!(future.as_mut().poll(&mut cx), task::Poll::Ready(10));\n562:     /// ```\n563:     #[inline]\n564:     #[must_use]\n565:     #[stable(feature = \"noop_waker\", since = \"1.85.0\")]\n566:     #[rustc_const_stable(feature = \"noop_waker\", since = \"1.85.0\")]\n567:     pub const fn noop() -> &'static Waker {\n568:         const WAKER: &Waker = &Waker { waker: RawWaker::NOOP };\n569:         WAKER\n570:     }\n571: \n572:     /// Gets the `data` pointer used to create this `Waker`.\n573:     #[inline]\n574:     #[must_use]\n575:     #[stable(feature = \"waker_getters\", since = \"1.83.0\")]\n576:     pub fn data(&self) -> *const () {\n577:         self.waker.data\n578:     }\n579: \n580:     /// Gets the `vtable` pointer used to create this `Waker`.\n581:     #[inline]\n582:     #[must_use]\n583:     #[stable(feature = \"waker_getters\", since = \"1.83.0\")]\n584:     pub fn vtable(&self) -> &'static RawWakerVTable {\n585:         self.waker.vtable\n586:     }\n587: \n588:     /// Constructs a `Waker` from a function pointer.\n589:     #[inline]\n590:     #[must_use]\n591:     #[unstable(feature = \"waker_from_fn_ptr\", issue = \"148457\")]\n592:     pub const fn from_fn_ptr(f: fn()) -> Self {\n593:         // SAFETY: Unsafe is used for transmutes, pointer came from `fn()` so it\n594:         //         is sound to transmute it back to `fn()`.\n595:         static VTABLE: RawWakerVTable = unsafe {\n596:             RawWakerVTable::new(\n597:                 |this| RawWaker::new(this, &VTABLE),\n598:                 |this| transmute::<*const (), fn()>(this)(),\n599:                 |this| transmute::<*const (), fn()>(this)(),\n600:                 |_| {},\n601:             )\n602:         };\n603:         let raw = RawWaker::new(f as *const (), &VTABLE);\n604: \n605:         // SAFETY: `clone` is just a copy, `drop` is a no-op while `wake` and\n606:         //         `wake_by_ref` just call the function pointer.\n607:         unsafe { Self::from_raw(raw) }\n608:     }\n609: }\n610: \n611: #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n612: impl Clone for Waker {\n613:     #[inline]\n614:     fn clone(&self) -> Self {\n615:         Waker {\n616:             // SAFETY: This is safe because `Waker::from_raw` is the only way\n617:             // to initialize `clone` and `data` requiring the user to acknowledge\n618:             // that the contract of [`RawWaker`] is upheld.\n619:             waker: unsafe { (self.waker.vtable.clone)(self.waker.data) },\n620:         }\n621:     }\n622: \n623:     /// Assigns a clone of `source` to `self`, unless [`self.will_wake(source)`][Waker::will_wake] anyway.\n624:     ///\n625:     /// This method is preferred over simply assigning `source.clone()` to `self`,\n626:     /// as it avoids cloning the waker if `self` is already the same waker.\n627:     ///\n628:     /// # Examples\n629:     ///\n630:     /// ```\n631:     /// use std::future::Future;\n632:     /// use std::pin::Pin;\n633:     /// use std::sync::{Arc, Mutex};\n634:     /// use std::task::{Context, Poll, Waker};\n635:     ///\n636:     /// struct Waiter {\n637:     ///     shared: Arc<Mutex<Shared>>,\n638:     /// }\n639: ();\n647:     ///     fn poll(self: Pin<&mut Self>, cx: &mut Context<'_>) -> Poll<()> {\n648:     ///         let mut shared = self.shared.lock().unwrap();\n649:     ///\n650:     ///         // update the waker\n651:     ///         shared.waker.clone_from(cx.waker());\n652:     ///\n653:     ///         // readiness logic ...\n654:     /// #       Poll::Ready(())\n655:     ///     }\n656:     /// }\n657:     ///\n658:     /// ```\n659:     #[inline]\n660:     fn clone_from(&mut self, source: &Self) {\n661:         if !self.will_wake(source) {\n662:             *self = source.clone();\n663:         }\n664:     }\n665: }\n666: \n667: #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n668: impl Drop for Waker {\n669:     #[inline]\n670:     fn drop(&mut self) {\n671:         // SAFETY: This is safe because `Waker::from_raw` is the only way\n672:         // to initialize `drop` and `data` requiring the user to acknowledge\n673:         // that the contract of `RawWaker` is upheld.\n674:         unsafe { (self.waker.vtable.drop)(self.waker.data) }\n675:     }\n676: }\n677: \n678: #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n679: impl fmt::Debug for Waker {\n680:     fn fmt(&self, f: &mut fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> fmt::Result {\n681:         let vtable_ptr = self.waker.vtable as *const RawWakerVTable;\n682:         f.debug_struct(\"Waker\")\n683:             .field(\"data\", &self.waker.data)\n684:             .field(\"vtable\", &vtable_ptr)\n685:             .finish()\n686:     }\n687: }\n688: \n689: /// A `LocalWaker` is analogous to a [`Waker`], but it does not implement [`Send`] or [`Sync`].\n690: ///\n691: /// This handle encapsulates a [`RawWaker`] instance, which defines the\n692: /// executor-specific wakeup behavior.\n693: ///\n694: /// Local wakers can be requested from a `Context` with the [`local_waker`] method.\n695: ///\n696: /// The typical life of a `LocalWaker` is that it is constructed by an executor, wrapped in a\n697: /// [`Context`] using [`ContextBuilder`], then passed to [`Future::poll()`]. Then, if the future chooses to return\n698: /// [`Poll::Pending`], it must also store the waker somehow and call [`LocalWaker::wake()`] when\n699: /// the future should be polled again.\n700: ///\n701: /// Implements [`Clone`], but neither [`Send`] nor [`Sync`]; therefore, a local waker may\n702: /// not be moved to other threads. In general, when deciding to use wakers or local wakers,\n703: /// local wakers are preferable unless the waker needs to be sent across threads. This is because\n704: /// wakers can incur in additional cost related to memory synchronization.\n705: ///\n706: /// Note that it is preferable to use `local_waker.clone_from(&new_waker)` instead\n707: /// of `*local_waker = new_waker.clone()`, as the former will avoid cloning the waker\n708: /// unnecessarily if the two wakers [wake the same task](Self::will_wake).\n709: ///\n710: /// # Examples\n711: /// Usage of a local waker to implement a future analogous to `std::thread::yield_now()`.\n712: /// ```\n713: /// #![feature(local_waker)]\n714: /// use std::future::{Future, poll_fn};\n715: /// use std::task::Poll;\n716: ///\n717: /// // a future that returns pending once.\n718: /// fn yield_now() -> impl Future<Output=()> + Unpin {\n719: ///     let mut yielded = false;\n720: ///     poll_fn(move |cx| {\n721: ///         if !yielded {\n722: ///             yielded = true;\n723: ///             cx.local_waker().wake_by_ref();\n724: ///             return Poll::Pending;\n725: ///         }\n726: ///         return Poll::Ready(())\n727: ///     })\n728: /// }\n729: ///\n730: /// # async fn __() {\n731: /// yield_now().await;\n732: /// # }\n733: /// ```\n734: ///\n735: /// [`Future::poll()`]: core::future::Future::poll\n736: /// [`Poll::Pending`]: core::task::Poll::Pending\n737: /// [`local_waker`]: core::task::Context::local_waker\n738: #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n739: #[repr(transparent)]\n740: pub struct LocalWaker {\n741:     waker: RawWaker,\n742: }\n743: \n744: #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n745: impl Unpin for LocalWaker {}\n746: \n747: impl LocalWaker {\n748:     /// Wakes up the task associated with this `LocalWaker`.\n749:     ///\n750:     /// As long as the executor keeps running and the task is not finished, it is\n751:     /// guaranteed that each invocation of [`wake()`](Self::wake) (or\n752:     /// [`wake_by_ref()`](Self::wake_by_ref)) will be followed by at least one\n753:     /// [`poll()`] of the task to which this `LocalWaker` belongs. This makes\n754:     /// it possible to temporarily yield to other tasks while running potentially\n755:     /// unbounded processing loops.\n756:     ///\n757:     /// Note that the above implies that multiple wake-ups may be coalesced into a\n758:     /// single [`poll()`] invocation by the runtime.\n759:     ///\n760:     /// Also note that yielding to competing tasks is not guaranteed: it is the\n761:     /// executor\u2019s choice which task to run and the executor may choose to run the\n762:     /// current task again.\n763:     ///\n764:     /// [`poll()`]: crate::future::Future::poll\n765:     #[inline]\n766:     #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n767:     pub fn wake(self) {\n768:         // The actual wakeup call is delegated through a virtual function call\n769:         // to the implementation which is defined by the executor.\n770: \n771:         // Don't call `drop` -- the waker will be consumed by `wake`.\n772:         let this = ManuallyDrop::new(self);\n773: \n774:         // SAFETY: This is safe because `Waker::from_raw` is the only way\n775:         // to initialize `wake` and `data` requiring the user to acknowledge\n776:         // that the contract of `RawWaker` is upheld.\n777:         unsafe { (this.waker.vtable.wake)(this.waker.data) };\n778:     }\n779: \n780:     /// Wakes up the task associated with this `LocalWaker` without consuming the `LocalWaker`.\n781:     ///\n782:     /// This is similar to [`wake()`](Self::wake), but may be slightly less efficient in\n783:     /// the case where an owned `Waker` is available. However, if this function\n799:     /// returns `true`, it is guaranteed that the `Waker`s will awaken the same task.\n800:     ///\n801:     /// This function is primarily used for optimization purposes \u2014 for example,\n802:     /// this type's [`clone_from`](Self::clone_from) implementation uses it to\n803:     /// avoid cloning the waker when they would wake the same task anyway.\n804:     #[inline]\n805:     #[must_use]\n806:     #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n807:     pub fn will_wake(&self, other: &LocalWaker) -> bool {\n808:         // We optimize this by comparing vtable addresses instead of vtable contents.\n809:         // This is permitted since the function is documented as best-effort.\n810:         let RawWaker { data: a_data, vtable: a_vtable } = self.waker;\n811:         let RawWaker { data: b_data, vtable: b_vtable } = other.waker;\n812:         a_data == b_data && ptr::eq(a_vtable, b_vtable)\n813:     }\n814: \n815:     /// Creates a new `LocalWaker` from the provided `data` pointer and `vtable`.\n816:     ///\n817:     /// The `data` pointer can be used to store arbitrary data as required\n818:     /// by the executor. For each\n824:     /// operation on the `LocalWaker`, the associated function in the `vtable`\n825:     /// will be called.\n826:     ///\n827:     /// # Safety\n828:     ///\n829:     /// The behavior of the returned `Waker` is undefined if the contract defined\n830:     /// in [`RawWakerVTable`]'s documentation is not upheld.\n831:     ///\n832:     #[inline]\n833:     #[must_use]\n834:     #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n835:     pub const unsafe fn new(data: *const (), vtable: &'static RawWakerVTable) -> Self {\n836:         LocalWaker { waker: RawWaker { data, vtable } }\n837:     }\n838: \n839:     /// Creates a new `LocalWaker` from [`RawWaker`].\n840:     ///\n841:     /// The behavior of the returned `LocalWaker` is undefined if the contract defined\n842:     /// in [`RawWaker`]'s and [`RawWakerVTable`]'s documentation is not upheld.\n843:     /// Therefore this method is unsafe.\n844:     #[inline]\n845:     #[must_use]\n846:     #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n847:     pub const unsafe fn from_raw(waker: RawWaker) -> LocalWaker {\n848:         Self { waker }\n849:     }\n850: \n851:     /// Returns a reference to a `LocalWaker` that does nothing when used.\n852:     ///\n853:     // Note!  Much of the documentation for this method is duplicated\n854:     // in the docs for `Waker::noop`.\n855:     // If you edit it, consider editing the other copy too.\n856:     //\n857:     /// This is mostly useful for writing tests that need a [`Context`] to poll\n858:     /// some futures, but are not expecting those futures to wake the waker or\n859:     /// do not need to do anything specific    /// So it should only be used when such a notification will not be needed to make progress.\n864:     ///\n865:     /// If an owned `LocalWaker` is needed, `clone()` this one.\n866:     ///\n867:     /// # Examples\n868:     ///\n869:     /// ```\n870:     /// #![feature(local_waker)]\n871:     /// use std::future::Future;\n872:     /// use std::task::{ContextBuilder, LocalWaker, Waker,     }\n888: \n889:     /// Gets the `data` pointer used to create this `LocalWaker`.\n890:     #[inline]\n891:     #[must_use]\n892:     #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue =   }\n904: \n905:     /// Constructs a `LocalWaker` from a function pointer.\n906:     #[inline]\n907:     #[must_use]\n908:     #[unstable(feature = \"waker_from_fn_ptr\", issue = \"148457\")]\n909: An executor can define an\\n22: /// implementation of this trait, and use that to construct a [`Waker`] to pass\\n23: /// to the tasks that are executed on that executor.\\n24: ///\\n25: /// This trait is a memory-safe and ergonomic alternative to constructing a\\n26: /// [`RawWaker`]. Some executors (especially\\n28: /// those for embedded systems) cannot use this API, which is why [`RawWaker`]\\n29: /// exists as an alternative for those systems.\\n30: ///\\n31: /// To construct a [`Waker`] from some type `W` implementing this trait,\\n32: /// wrap it in an [`Arc<W>`](Arc) and call `Waker::from()` on that.\\n33: /// It is also possible to convert to [`RawWaker`] in the same way.\\n34: ///\\n35: /// <!-- Ideally we'd link to the `From` impl, but rustdoc doesn't generate any page for it within\\n36: ///      `alloc` because `alloc` neither defines nor re-exports `From` or `Waker`, and we can't\\n37: ///      link ../../std/task/struct.Waker.html#impl-From%3CArc%3CW,+Global%3E%3E-for-Waker\\n38: ///      without getting a link-checking error in CI. -->\\n39: ///\\n40: /// # Examples\\n41: ///\\n42: /// A basic `block_on` function that takes a future and runs it to completion on\\n43: /// the current thread.\\n44: ///\\n45: /// **Note:** This example trades correctness for simplicity. ```rust\\n50: /// use std::future::Future;\\n51: /// use std::sync::Arc;\\n52: /// use std::task::{Context, Poll, Wake};\\n53: /// use std::thread::{self, Thread};\\n54: /// use core::pin::pin;\\n55: Additionally, it saves calls\\n187: /// to `Arc::clone`, which requires atomic synchronization.\\n188: ///\\n189: ///\\n190: /// # Examples\\n191: ///\\n192: /// This is a simplified example of a `spawn` and a `block_on` function. The `spawn` function\\n193: /// is used to push new tasks onto the run queue, while the block on function will remove them\\n194: /// and poll them. When a task is woken, it will put itself back on the run queue to be polled\\n195: /// by the executor.\\n196: ///\\n197: /// **Note:** This example trades correctness for simplicity. A real world example would interleave\\n198: /// poll calls with calls to an io reactor to wait for events instead of spinning on a loop.\\n199: ///\\n200: /// ```rust\\n201: /// /// use std::cell::RefCell;\\n207: /// use std::collections::VecDeque;\\n208: ///\\n209: ///\\n210: /// thread_local! {\\n211: ///     // A queue containing all tasks ready to do progress\\n212: /// });\\n235: /// }\\n236: ///\\n237: /// fn block_on<F>(future: F)\\n238: /// where\\n239: ///     F: Future<Output=()> + 'static + Sync + Send\\n240: /// {\\n241: ///     spawn(future);\\n242: /// implementation residing in library/core/src/task/wake.rs and library/alloc/src/task.rs.\\n\\nThe mechanism consists of several key components:\\n\\n1. **RawWaker and RawWakerVTable** (library/core/src/task/wake.rs, lines 22-204): These form the low-level foundation of the waker system. RawWaker is a data structure containing a data pointer and a vtable of function pointers. RawWakerVTable defines four unsafe function pointers: clone, wake, wake_by_ref, and drop. These functions are called to manage the lifecycle and wakeup behavior of tasks.\\n\\n2. **Waker type** (library/core/src/task/wake.rs, lines 405-609): A higher-level wrapper around RawWaker that implements Send and Sync traits. It provides safe methods like wake() (line 438) and wake_by_ref() (line 458) that delegate to the vtable functions. The Waker type also implements Clone (lines 612-665) with a clone_from optimization.\\n\\n3. **LocalWaker type** (library/core/src/task/wake.rs, lines 738-981): Similar to Waker but without Send/Sync requirements, allowing it to hold non-thread-safe data like Rc<T>. It provides the same wake() and wake_by_ref() interface.\\n\\n4. **Context and ContextBuilder** (library/core/src/task/wake.rs, lines 212-376): Context wraps references to both Waker and LocalWaker, providing the execution context passed to Future::poll(). ContextBuilder allows constructing Context with optional extension data.\\n\\n5. **Wake and LocalWake traits** (library/alloc/src/task.rs, lines 90-350): These traits provide a memory-safe interface for implementing custom wakers. The Wake trait requires an Arc<Self> and is implemented with raw_waker() (lines 136-177) which constructs the RawWaker vtable. Similarly, LocalWake uses Rc<Self> with local_raw_waker() (lines 314-350).\\n\\n6. **Poll enum** (library/core/src/task/poll.rs, lines 14-28): Defines the two outcomes of polling a future: Ready(T) or Pending. This enum is the return type of Future::poll().\\n\\n7. **Future trait** (library/core/src/future/future.rs, lines 37-114): The core trait with a single method poll(self: Pin<&mut Self>, cx: &mut Context<'_>) -> Poll<Self::Output>. The documentation (lines 43-114) explains the polling mechanism and waker interaction pattern.\\n\\n8. **poll_fn function** (library/core/src/future/poll_fn.rs, lines 6-70): Creates a future from a closure that receives a Context parameter, allowing manual poll implementation.\\n\\n9. **ready! macro** (library/core/src/task/ready.rs, lines 50-57): Utility macro that extracts the value from Poll::Ready or returns Poll::Pending early.\\n\\n10. **Future module exports** (library/core/src/future/mod.rs, lines 12-68): Exports the Future trait and related types like ResumeTy used internally for .await desugaring.\\n\\nThe polling loop works as follows: An executor repeatedly polls a pinned future with a Context containing a Waker. When the future isn't ready, it returns Poll::Pending and stores a clone of the Waker. When the underlying I/O or other event completes, the Waker's wake() or wake_by_ref() method is called, which invokes the appropriate vtable function to notify the executor to re-poll the future. This design allows efficient, callback-free async programming in Rust.\"\n}\n",

RawWaker is a data structure containing a data pointer and a vtable of function pointers. RawWakerVTable defines four unsafe function pointers: clone, wake, wake_by_ref, and drop. These functions are called to manage the lifecycle and wakeup behavior of tasks.\\n\\n2. **Waker type** (library/core/src/task/wake.rs, lines 405-609): A higher-level wrapper around RawWaker that implements Send and Sync traits. It provides safe methods like wake() (line 438) and wake_by_ref() (line 458) that delegate to the vtable functions.
